Dear Thomas,

You are probably right. I have no objection to put all
participants on this paper. I wrote what I regarded as relevant.
Donatella once promised to provide the literature survey?
May be some other partner would make a general introduction?
I hope I did not forget any one of the members. I don't think
there is any point in more or less contribution. All participants have
contributed significantly.

For me the message of this work is clear. Integration of core
ontologies is a demanding intellectual and time-consuming task.
I think the method and experience applies to any such work.
I don't think it applies to terminology on Eleonore Rosch's base
level. Core ontologies are fairly different.
Personally, I have hardly time to invest more in this report.

Please proceed as you regard appropriate.

best wishes,

Martin

Thomas Baker wrote:

> Dear Martin, dear Vittore,
> 
> Many thanks for the draft.  I am glad that the process yielded
> a result with which you are happy.  As a deliverable for DELOS,
> however, I think it will need some additional work, at least
> on the presentation and "spin" of the paper as a whole.
> 
> One important point is that the purpose of DELOS is to promote
> networking of European researchers; the support for meetings
> is supposed to lead to a result that represents a collective
> effort.  As presented, it is a paper by a single author.
> Is there any reason we could not cast you as the Editor
> (or some other appropriate title) of a paper of the DELOS
> Working Group on Ontology Harmonisation and list all of the
> participants in the process somewhere?  If the participants did
> not all contribute equally, or even if there was disagreement
> about the scope and methods, this could perhaps be discussed
> somewhere in the text.
> 
> Also, might it be possible to cast this exercise as an
> example of the sort of intellectual work that needs to
> be done in order to harmonise different ontology models?
> There should be some discussion of ontologies in a more
> general sense, with citations of related work.  Since these
> papers are supposed to be readable by non-specialists, this
> section should include two or three paragraphs explaining
> what ontologies are, why one wants to harmonise them, and
> what harmonisation means.
> 
> In a concluding section, perhaps there could be some more
> general reflection on the process of harmonisation.  If the
> process you followed in the working group was "extraordinarily
> successful", are there lessons of a process nature that can
> be gleaned for groups wishing to undertake a similar task?
> 
> I see from the Minutes that you are planning to work on this
> further, for example with Jane and Carl for a JoDI paper.
> If the group decided not to write a White Paper, the two
> (or four) of us still need to work with what is there and do
> our best to turn this into an acceptable DELOS deliverable.
> I am of course willing to put editorial effort into this as 
> well.  Vittore, what is your opinion?
> 
> Cheers,
> Tom
> 
> On Fri, Aug 02, 2002 at 09:13:26PM +0300, Martin Doerr wrote:
> 
>>I add a summary which I hope is satisfactory for a final report for DELOS
>>you were asking for.
>>We decided not to produce the White Paper, but a publication of me,
>>Jane and Carl on the experience and outcome of the process. Reason:
>>many initial participants actually did not intend to work for such a WhitePaper.
>>I attach also the minutes.
>>
>>I think the whole process was extraordinarily successful.
>>
>>All the best,
>>
>>Martin
>>
